text:
Excellent recipe--but I don't know that I would've given it 5 stars without the addition of 1 can each of black and garbanzo beans.  It needed a little more "body" and the beans were just the thing. Probably a can of corn in place of one of the beans would've worked well also.  The spices were perfect--however, I always like a touch of sweetness to tomato based recipes, so I added 1/4 cup of brown sugar....YUM! I would highly recommend this chili recipe---and for anyone that never usually tries ground turkey in place of ground beef, believe me, you'll never miss it.

text:
What a great way to warm up on a cold night! We like our chili with beans, so I added a can of kidney and pinto beans. We also like our chili very spicy, so I added chili powder and a minced jalapeno. The salsa I used was spicy, too. I really liked the zucchini in this! I browned the turkey then threw everything into the slow cooker for 5 hours on high. I added some cornstarch after a few hours because the chili was too runny for me. Next time I will add more vegetables, because I like it really chunky.

city:

region:

country:

text:
Very Nice recipe!  I made some modifications to it and it turned out wonderful.  A can of beef broth here (Canada) is 10 oz not 14 and I used a whole large can (28 oz) of diced tomatoes in place of 14 oz can of crushed.  Tomatoes are the base of the chili in my opinion and to forgo a large quantity and big chucky ones I think would be a mistake.  I added all the vegetables that were called for but in addition I also added 2 chopped carrots, 3 stalks of chopped celery, and an 8oz packaged of sliced mushrooms.  I too like thick chili and although I LOVE beans (especially kidney) I am trying a carb reduced diet (P90X!) and beans unfortnately are high on the list despite their other healthy and nutritious qualities!  By adding the other vegetables, the chili thickened up just how I like it and tasted great!!  I also did not have any green chili pepper so substitued with chili powder (1/4 cup).  I also added 1/2 teaspoon of garlic, 1 teaspoon of basil, about 1 teaspoon of salt and 1 teaspoon of sugar to get rid of that bland taste that tomato paste usually has!  I also added half a can of light beer (i.e. Coors Light or Bud Light etc), yes beer!, as it gives chili that extra oomph!  I topped with fat free sour cream and reduced fat cheddar cheese.  YUM!  I would like to try this with the green chili beans next time but I think I will keep everything else the same.  Thank you SO much for sharing this delicious, healthy, recipe!

text:
I must admit, I took some liberties with this recipe, but it turned out very well!  The main thing I did was use ground beef, rather than turkey.  We prefer beef and the rest of the recipe looked so good, I took a chance with it.  I also upped the tomato paste and lessened the beef broth, because the chili was so runny, and still had to strain out some liquid to have a chili rather than a soup.  I did not cook the beef in vegetable oil either and left out the zucchini completely.  When it was all done I let it simmer on low for 30 minutes and the flavors came together wonderfully!  I served it with cheddar garlic biscuits and we had a great meal!  Will definitely make again!

Considering that I'm not usually a huge fan of chili, this was TO DIE FOR!!! All I've eaten for the last two days is this chili, I can't get enough of it. I also made a few changes. I added some chili powder (about 1/2 tablespoon), some portobello mushrooms (I happened to have some that were going bad and decided to throw them in) and about a tablespoon of chopped garlic. I also added a can of kidney beans with their liquid, and a whole can of tomato paste instead of just a tablespoon. I didn't have chile peppers so I added one jalapeno. All together, it's absolutely amazing. I don't doubt it's just as amazing without my adjustments, I just had a few extras laying around I needed to use up, so I threw them in. Will definitely make again! Thanks!

Weight Watchers people~ about 6 points per bowl (a good helping) if you use x-tra lean ground turkey. This doesn't include the sour cream and cheese on top. I even added a can of black beans, and a can of chili beans. To make servings bigger, add more 0 point veggies like mushrooms and bell pepper. I've lost 60 pounds on Weight Watchers, and I am extremely careful about calculating points, so you can trust me! ;)

text:
My husband loves chili and we are always looking for good ground turkey recipes so we're happy to have found this one.  I made some changes based on other reviews and what we had on hand.  Instead of 3 zucchinis I used one, a can of corn (drained) and a can of chili beans (not drained).  Instead of chopped tomatoes in puree and a can of green chiles, I used a can of tomatoes and chiles together.  We didn't have coriander or pepper flakes so I skipped those, and it was plenty spicy.  To reduce the amount of dirty dishes I sauteed the veggies together first, then cooked the meat (with salt and pepper and garlic) and added the veggies.  Served with grated cheddar and cornbread, and my husband and I both agreed it was better the next day!  Thanks!

I added garbanzo beans and black beans and cooked a little longer to boil off some of the water. I cooked it for about 2 hours total. My only minor gripe is that the use of the taco seasoning (obviously) lends this chili more of a taco flavor than of the typical Cumin flavor of most chili. Don't get me wrong, the taste is still great and the amount of spice is perfect for me. If you want to judge the flavor based on that of a more typical chili though, you might want to make some spice substitutions. Overall though, it was still a great meal and leftovers were great too.

I used 2 lbs turkey, 2 large onions, 6 really small peppers, the whole small can of tomato paste, none of the chili pepper flakes or chiles (I can't eat spicy foods), a big can of crushed tomatoes, 4 cans of different beans and garlic. Everything else was the same. I cooked the onions, turkey, peppers, zucchini and garlic in a big pot until the turkey was brown, drained, then tossed it all in the crockpot for 4 hours on high. It was soooo good! Will be eating this for days. Thanks for such a great recipe!

text:
I was hungry for chili but wanted something different than my usual recipe.  I'm a big fan of ground turkey so when I saw this one it was a must-try.  The title is well-earned "Terrific" because it is just that.  I only used one pound of turkey and it was plenty (I like lots of meat so another 1/2 pound would have been too much) The addition of taco seasoning is by far one of the best ingredients in my opinion.  I used a homemade taco seasoning from this site that is amazing and I will never use another.  I had to add kidney beans like other reviewers because I love my chili with beans.  I did the directions differently and didn't use the oil at all.  I find that with ground turkey, if you cook it on a low medium setting it doesn't cook too fast and doesn't stick.  So I browned the turkey along with onions, two large cloves garlic, green peppers and added the seasonings.  When that was cooked I added the beef broth, crushed tomatoes and kidney beans.  I didn't have zucchini and didn't bother with the sour cream and cheese.  It was good enough without the garnish (and extra calories) This was exactly the recipe I was looking for - full of flavor and a comfort food all rolled into one.  Thanks for a great recipe!

city:

text:
This recipe earned thumbs up from an entire Christmas party. I do a lot of different kinds of hunting during the winter, and I needed a recipe to use for some wild Canada Goose. I've listed all the substitutions are variations I used. The majority of my guests, like myself, like spicy cajun food, so I went with that theme.  I chopped 3 goose breasts into small cubes to substitute for the turkey, and used a bag of Tex-Mex chili seasoning instead of taco mix. Instead of the crushed tomatoes, I used a can of Medium-Spice Rotel tomatoes, and also added a can of chili beans and 3 freshly chopped jalapenos. I reduced the zucchini from 3 down to 1, and added 1/2 of a yellow squash for color. Instead of the chili pepper flakes (who sells those??) I used red pepper flakes, and I added about a teaspoon and a half of 50/50 Cayenne and Chili powder mix.  I followed the rest of the recipe until completion, and then refridgerated the chili overnight. I woke up the next day and put the chili in the crock pot on "Warm" for about 8 hours to really let the peppers release their warmth. All our guests were dumbfounded to learn they'd eaten, and LOVED, wild game, especially wild game with a not so great plate-reputation.

Very simple. I had been looking for a chili recipe for awhile. I've never made it, and it was easier than I thought! I added the tomato paste and seasonings, and it colored the ground turkey, so I was worried if I browned it enough, but I figured it would cook while I stewed it with the rest of the ingredients.  I couldn't find zucchini, so I left that part out. I doubled the recipe because it was easier, I could only find a 28 ounce can of crushed tomatoes, a 14 ounce of salsa and I didn't want to waste a 6oz can of tomato paste, so I just used it all.  It tasted delicious! I can't believe I spent $2.50 a cup of chili at Quiznos when I can make it myself with unlimited "refills"! The flavor was very good. I added cayenne pepper to the onions and green pepper as I was sauteeing them, to give it more spice. I also added a can of black beans 30 minutes before turning off the heat.   If anyone could help me, how can you thicken the base? I tried adding cornstarch mixed with water, but I was afraid to add too much cornstarch, so it made the chili MORE runny because of the addition of more water. After stewing though, some water evaporated and it was okay. It wasn't the right consistency I was hoping for, but it was very delicious. My picky eater of a brother loves it! :] Thanks!

text:
I almost never follow a recipe exactly as written.  I believe that recipes are a guideline and everyone adjusts it according to what they have on hand and to their personal tastes as well.  With that being said this recipe was a very good starting point and I am only posting my changes for my own reference later on.  

I used boneless chicken thighs and breast bc that was what I had in the freezer.  I would have loved to try the zucchini but had none.  I added a can of black beans, light kidney beans, and some leftover corn from the night before.  I diced an onion, a green pepper, several cloves of garlic and a stalk of celery and sautÃ©ed them in some vegetable oil.  Then I sautÃ©ed the chicken which I had cut into bite sized pieces.  Threw all of that in the crockpot and added the seasoning.  I made my own taco seasoning from this site bc I didn't have any of the packaged kind and left out the coriander (I don't even know what it is).
Next I added one can of diced tomatoes, one can of tomatoes with green chiles, the salsa, and a small jar of homemade v8 juice. Next came the beans and corn.  I did not use beef broth but added a couple of tsp of chicken bouillon base ( with no sodium, this recipe does not need any added salt bc there is plenty in the taco seasoning).  Cooked for 3-4 hrs on high then tasted it.  It was nearly perfect at this point but tasted very acidic to me from the tomatoes so I threw in a little brown sugar.  It is now the perfect pot of soup. 5+ stars.

Toasted some hot dog buns, topped the dogs with this chili, jack/chedder cheese and red onions and O BOY! was it good. My husband's new favorite chili and he LOVES beef chili.

text:
This is the first time I've made chilli. My husband hates beans, so it never occurred to me to find a recipes without beans. We are also trying to reduce his intake of red meat. This recipe was perfect! I made a few modifications - I left out the coriander, because I didn't have any, but I did add crushed garlic. I used homemade taco seasoning because I make it sodium-free (A salt-free version of Allrecipes Taco Seasoning I). I used "no salt added" fat free beef broth. I used sweet corn instead of zucchini. We added crushed tortilla chips on top. I accidentally bought hot salsa, and it really gave tons of heat to this recipe. My husband loved it, but next time, I think I'll go for medium, because my mouth was burning! The cheese and sour cream helped put the fire out Other than that, I followed the recipe and it turned out great. I plan to freeze the leftovers in 1-2 portion servings and use it for quick lunches.

text:
My husband and kids say this is the best chili they've ever eaten! They were amazed to find out it was made with ingredients they normally don't enjoy. I thinly sliced zucchini, yellow squash, onion & yellow bell pepper, which I added to the ground turkey, as it was cooking. I added just a bit of water to the mix, keeping the turkey from clumping. My kids are major bean fans, so I added a can of ranch style pinto beans w/jalapeno's, chili beans & black beans. I used fire roasted diced tomatoes with onions & garlic. I didn't have beef broth, so substituted chicken broth. I served over chips, topped with shredded cheddar cheese. I'm thrilled to have found a healthy version of chili. I will definitely be making this again. Thanks so much for sharing!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Such a great recipe! As others have suggested, it's a great base recipe that can be tweaked to your own liking. I browned the turkey without the oil because I didn't feel it was necessary. I used some of the beef broth to mix with the taco seasoning to cook that in. From there, I just added the salsa and tomatoes and started simmering, throwing things in as I went. I used two 4oz cans of green chiles, half a jumbo white onion and an entire green pepper. I also threw in two stalks of chopped celery. I left out zucchini because I'm not a big fan, and added two cans of black beans because I love them. I think the best part was using two cans of fire roasted tomatoes instead of the other kind as suggested... it ended up with a nice, robust flavor! I also added a bottle of my favorite local beer, a malty sweet red that I thought would balance the acidity of the tomatoes. Beer may sound weird, but it comes out awesome! I used an entire 6oz can of tomato paste so I wouldn't waste it, and left out coriander because I didn't have any. Simmered for about 3-3.5 hours and the end result was to die for! I absolutely LOVED it and so did my friends and family! My mom said it was actually better than her own chili that I grew up on! A little cooking tip for the beginners like me... cooking with the lid off will remove more of the liquid and cook down into a thicker chili. If it is already thick enough, keep the lid on while it is simmering. Enjoy everyone, this is highly recommended!!

Sergey Potupchik

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Awesomely simple recipe, with lots of room for customization. By itself, it's a fantastic recipe, but the true strength lies in the ability to add things to your hearts content.
I personally doubled the recipe, and added the following ingrediants:
3 medium red peppers, diced; 3 medium carrots, diced; one red onion and one yellow onion (instead of two yellow), diced; 2 shallots, minced; 4 medium jalapenos (instead of canned green chili's); 1 can garbanzo beans; 1 can kidney beans;
Sauteed the carrots for about 5 minutes on high, stirring occasionally. Then added the green and red peppers for a few minutes, and finally threw the onions and shallots in to finish till they were translucent. Jalapeno's I threw in a pot with vinegar till it started boiling, then boiled for about 5 minutes. Take the peppers off the stove and blend them together with some fresh garlic and some of the crushed tomatos (adding some vinegar to get it to a slurry). Added all the veggies and jalapeno slurry at the time the recipe calls for (including the chick peas/beans), and moved to the crock pot on high for 2 hours. Add a water/flour slurry (approximately 1 tbsp of each, double that if a thicker chili is desired) to the crock pot, mix thoroughly, and cook on low overnight. I actually had about 3 lbs of jalapenos, so I made a lot of extra slurry on the side to add as desired. Plan on making it much more often now that I have this incredibly simple recipe (planned for Christmas dinner).

city:

region:

country:
None
text:
The ingredients regarding portion sizes available in stores here are as follows: Turkey - 20 oz. frozen; taco seasoning -- just add a pkg. rounded to an oz.; broth 14 - 20 oz. works fine; can up the broth in place of part of the water. In other words don't let larger purchased quantities go to waste. A little more here or there makes no taste difference.

The arrangement of this recipe should be changed as follows: Chop the vegetables first. Brown the turkey. Add ALL spices and the broth -- bring to a boil and then simmer 4 minutes. Now, in your empty skillet, brown the onions and pepper. Toss into a kettle along with the turkey. 
Bring to a simmer. Brown the zuke. Toss into kettle. 

Now for added pleasure, as one remarkable woman suggested, add 3 minced garlic simmered just briefly. Add a cup or so of frozen corn. Add a can of black beans (rinsed). Add a tablespoon of brown sugar. Stir.

Now, everything should be in the kettle that has been simmering. Simmer an additional 15 minutes. Now wasn't that easy and well organized? 

Smiling right at you, Vaughn

This recipe is awesome!!  We love it and now it's a family staple.  I even served it to my son's cub scout campout and a few people said it was the best chili they had ever had.  The changes I made are as follows:  I left out the zucchini, added both a can of each black beans and kidney beans (drained and rinsed) and added minced garlic.  I browned the turkey in a skillet and added it, and all the remaining ingredients to a crock pot and cooked on low for 4-5 hours or high for 2-3 hours.  Very tasty!

After trying this recipe.. i will never try another chili recipe. This was literally the first time I ever attempted to make chili and it was a success! I did make a few adjustments. I used 1/2 tsp of coriander and 1/2 tsp of cumin because I love cumin and didn't really know what coriander tastes like. I also left out the tomato paste and used a splash of the beef broth to mix in the spices. I used 2 onions because my fiance and I LOVE onions. I also added 1 can of black beans and 1 can of kidney beans.. then threw it all into the crockpot for a few hours after it was all combined! Next time I will do a can of chili beans instead of kidney beans. My chili recipe for life! Thanks for sharing!!

Really great, really easy, really healthy recipe.  I agree with many other reviewers in that a couple additions are necessary.  I added 1 can of corn and 1 can of kidney beans, but any bean would work.  I did fully brown the meat and add the can of beef broth before adding the spices (taco seasonings thru pepper flakes) as I felt the spices without the broth would burn the pan.  I do advise cooking it several hours in advance and letting it simmer so favors can mix.  I also added a couple shakes of Tabasco as I like spicy.  Thank you Big Surprise for a great recipe that's a keeper!

Great recipe, especially good for using up extra zukes from the garden.  A few additions really upped the ante and added complexity to the flavor:  I added 3 cloves of crushed garlic, 1 tsp of cumin, 1 tsp of chipotle spice, 1 bottle of beer, 1 Tbsp each of worchestershire and tamari sauce,  1 can each of whote and red kidney beans, 1 can chickpeas, 1 can black beans, 1 small can of tomato paste, some chopped tomatoes I had hanging around the kitchen, 1 cup of leftover coffee and 1 small can of tomato sauce to thicken. I also browned the turkey with some chopped hickory bacon.  After browning the meat, I added everything else in no particular order, except for the tomato sauce and paste which I added at the end (just add what you need).

For the most part I stayed true to the recipe. I did double the recipe and add two cans kidney beans, one can garbanzo beans and a can of black beans. I also added more beef broth to loosen it up a bit. It was incredible!!! If your not a turkey lover I encourage you to try it with turkey before you use ground beef because the flavor is so rich that you cant even tell that it is made with turkey. Top with shredded cheddar cheese and enjoy!!

text:
Best chili I've ever made.  I omitted the green chilis as I couldn't find any in the store.  I added the spices and tomato paste to the meat at the early stage of browning as the recipe was unclear if spices went in before, during, or after browning.  It made the meat really finely crumbled and delicious.  I also added two cans of rinsed and drained beans at the final stage with the zucchini.  I used sodium reduced taco seasoning and broth to shave out some salt, and make the dish even healthier.

My husband and I found this recipe to be extremely salty. Taco seasonong mix is loaded with sodium, and all the canned ingredients have their own salt, especially the salsa & broth. When this was done it was too salty for us to eat. You can always add salt to taste at the end.

My family loved this chili! I did make some changes... left out the zucchini and green bell peppers (my kids don't like them) and left out the coriander (we didn't have it). I also added a can of kidney beans, a can of garbanzo beans, 2 tbsp. of brown sugar, and 2 tbsp. of plain greek yogurt (sour cream would have worked the same). It was perfect for adults!!! So yummy! Next time I'll make it without the chili flakes in order to tone down the spice for my kids. I may also put the onions in the food processor instead of chopping them and do a 4oz. can of diced green chilis instead of 7oz because of the kids. Such an  easy and healthy recipe.

I make this every year in anticipation of my out of towners coming in for the holiday. I  double it and scoop the chili into gallon zip lock bags and store flat in the freezer.

text:
Really good. I wanted to throw something in the Crockpot in the morning, so I started with this recipe. I omitted the bell pepper because I was lazy, used hot/spicy taco seasoning mix, added two drained cans of kidney beans, used vegetable broth instead of beef because that is what I had open, and omitted the tomato paste. I wish I had added the tomato paste to give the broth a little more tomato taste and thickness and will use it next time. I also did not brown the turkey first, as is usually advised for these kind of recipes. I think that may be why the final result looked a little strange, but it tasted great. A great flavor, some heat but not too spicy. It looks like a complicated recipe, because it has so many ingredients, but mostly it is just opening cans/jars and adding spices. If I make it in the Crockpot again, I will add the zucchini later. I added it at the beginning, with everything else, and it was overcooked. Otherwise, really solid recipe, will definitely make again.

text:
This recipe is SO good! I made it for a group of friends last night and it was a huge hit!!! Everyone loved it and some even ate it with the "grandma's cornbread" mixed in!

I did change some things... as other reviewers have mentioned, I thought it helped to add a full can of tomato paste and some garlic. I also love beans in chili and decided to add one can of each pinto and black beans which really helped thicken out the chili! In addition, I added a full can of corn, a couple carrots, did just one larger zucchini, and did one red and one yellow bell pepper instead of the green.

I am sure you could customize this recipe a lot and it would be just as delicious! It just depends on your preferences. I think this was one of the best chilis I have ever had and would highly recommend trying it! It was great for the party too because I made it early in the afternoon and let it simmer until guests arrived... it had a chance to develop the flavors a little more and made the timing of feeding everyone a snap! Served it up with the "grandma's cornbread" recipe, and some cheddar cheese, sour cream, and sliced green onions. YUM!!! 

Will definitely be making this again! Thanks :)

text:
I made this recipe last night and I am VERY pleased with it. I am no chef by far and as I was cutting the vegetables up I got a chance to see that even more. I omitted some of the ingredients because my supermarket didn't have them (green onions, coriander, and tomato paste). I also forgot to add the diced tomatoes and I didn't have tomato paste so I used a small can of tomato sauce. Maybe there is a big difference but I doubt I would taste it as much. Also, I used a peppercorn blend that had coriander in it because there was no coriander available. Everything worked out well with cooking the ingredients together. The only thing I would say is if you don't like big chunks of veggies, make sure you dice everything up finely. My zucchini's were cut fairly big but it's fine now because they soften up after all the cooking is done and almost melt in your mouth. 

All in all, great recipe! And like someone said, it does make "tons" and is good to freeze for later if you want some for a night and then need to make something else for the next day.

text:
I've made this recipe twice now, and it has turned out amazing both times.  I never thought using canned and packaged ingredients could taste so fresh!

I had better results using the all white meat ground turkey (as opposed to the regular ground turkey with dark meat).  I used olive oil instead of veg. oil.  I also used two pounds of meat both times and omitted the onion and green bell pepper (personal preference).  I added two tablespoons of chili powder, a few dashes of cayenne pepper and extra of all the other spices.  At the end, if it's not thick enough, you can always stir in a tablespoon of flour or cornstarch mixed with cold water.

I also ran the chiles through the food processor for a less chunky texture and used a sweet salsa, I like a little sweet/spicy combo in my chili.  I added a can of corn to make up for the missing body (less chunks and no beans for me!).

Everyone loves this chili and I can't get enough - especially topped with low fat cheese and FF sour cream!

text:
This chili was so delicious. The only changes I made to the ingredients were adding an additional half pound of turkey (so 2 lbs total) and adding a can of IPA. 

Out of laziness I made this a one pot meal and it turned out perfectly. I sauteed the onion first, then the turkey then I added the zucchinni and garlic and spices. I used a full can of IPA that I had on hand to deglaze the pan before adding the other liquids. After that I followed the recipe instructions exactly but simmered for a long time. I wanted the zuchinni to get really soft so i could smash it and thicken the chili. 

Worked like a charm and will definitely be making this again!

I was so excited to make this because of all the rave reviews. I made it as instructed but added corn and black beans as recommended by others. I found the taste to be blah, just okay. I had to spice it up a bit on my own adding more salt, ground cumin and a few other additions. I think that there is too much broth in the recipe and it was very loose. It took a really long time for me to cook it down to reduce the liquid. Also, I think that the crushed tomatoes also gave too much liquid. I would use 2 cans of fire roasted diced tomatoes if I were to make this again and skip the salsa. I'm glad others liked this recipe but it just didn't cut the mustard for us.

text:
I am not a big fan of recipes that use packaged food products or seasoning mixes. This one asks you to chop fresh onions and peppers, but then wants you to dump in a jar of salsa?? Coriander powder, Chili pepper flakes and oregano then a pack of taco seasoning??    Redundant...   Oh, and chili without beans? come on.. A bag of red kidney beans re-hydrated and cooked while the veggies are cut, prepped and cooked.
Due to the above, I really only use this recipe as a general guide for the turkey/squash ratio.  I make a home made chili seasoning mix from multiple varieties of dried chilies, Mexican oregano and roasted cumin seed then measure it in, according to the meat volume. 
I have made this at least 4 times now, tripling the recipe each time because it is _that_good_  and freezes well.
Everyone who tries it loves it. The squash is a master stroke that keeps the turkey from getting dry and gritty.

text:
I have never made turkey chili before, but this stuff was very good! I did it a little different, as I cooked it in my Instant Pot. I sautÃ©ed the turkey with the spices &  tomato paste, added the beef stock, salsa, and then threw everything else in and set the Instant Pot on the "chili" program (high-pressure for 30 minutes). I am not a zucchini super-fan so I didn't know how that would turn out, however even with 3 zucchini, which seemed like a LOT, it really cooked down to a lot less, and you wouldn't even know that there was zucchini in there. Like other reviewers, I added a blended-up can of black beans for extra protein & fibre. I could not find pinto beans in the store (they're not common in central Canada), so I added a can of refried beans which are pinto beans ground up anyway. Worked like a charm. Will definitely make this again!

I didn't use the zucchini because they were past their prime upon further inspection.  Instead I added a can of rinsed dark kidney beans and a can of sliced mushrooms.  I also used chicken bone broth and added cumin.  Cooked it long enough to reduce out most of the liquid and then put in a 9x13 pan.  I mixed a box of jiffy corn mix with 1/2 cup sour cream, 3 eggs, 1/2 shredded cheddar cheese, and 3 green onions chopped and spread it on top of the chili.  Baked for 30 minutes at 350 or until corbread was golden brown.  So yummy!  Everyone loved it and I will definitely make again.

text:
This was delicious and most definitely terrific!  It was very easy to throw together and had a phenomenal flavor.  This is definitely up there with our top favorite chili recipes.  I did only use 1 lb. ground turkey, added in some chopped celery, a few chopped garlic cloves, and about 1/2 can of water added.  I also completely omitted step 3.  I found it unnecessary to saute the veggies separately and just sauteed them up with the meat mixture from the beginning.   I did add the zucchini near the last 20-30 minutes, so they wouldn't get too mushy, and only added 1 medium sized zucchini and it was plenty.   I simmered on the stove for around 1 1/2 hours and it was so full of flavor and delicious.  You don't miss the beans in this.  It's a great turkey veggie chili with a medium heat level.  Thank you for the recipe, it will definitely be made again!

text:
I've been making ground turkey chili for years in a crockpot,  I get a bit carried away,  I use one pound of ground turkey, black beans, pintos, red kidney and red beans. Along with my seasonings I add a tablespoon or two of peanut butter, this tweaks the flavor and if you over season the chili,  the peanut butter buffers the heat. I'd list the seasonings but I never make my chili the same way twice (I must be dyslexic or have a short attention span), I use a pinch of this, a fistful of that, a smidgen of whatever, a can of beer I just walk it through the spice garden !  Plus I git  1/2 crocked makin' crockpot chili !!! Bon Appetito,...Shalom !

it was ok but to be honest the beef broth did not go with the turkey meet.  I think water or chicken broth would be better.

i did this in the slow cooker, browned the meat first and then threw it all int he slow cooker for 2.5 hours on high and 1 hour on low. I had to use cumin instead of coriander since I didn't have any in the pantry, but it still tasted great!  If using the slow cooker, i recommend to chop the veggies bigger than usual because they turn mushy, but we like it that way. I also had to use onion powder to supplement b/c i didn't have enough onions. I thought it was too soupy, so i added extra tomato paste to thicken it up.  I also added half can of kidney beans - duh! Chili!

I really liked this chili. I never would have thought to add zucchini to chili. I changed a few things. text:
My first recipe and review on Allrecipes.com!  This chili was completely delicious!  I followed the recipe and made some additions based on the recommendations of other reviewers, such as one can each of black beans, and kidney beans (both drained), and increased the crushed tomato to a 28 oz can.  I also added two items from my kitchen that needed to be used up:  one tomato, chopped up, and roughly 1/3 cup of frozen corn kernels.  The amount of spices was perfect and did not need salt (I did not use low sodium broth, but did use low sodium crushed tomato, if that helps).  I did use about a half can (7 oz or so) of leftover chicken broth instead of water since the addition of the beans really thickened up the chili.  I love this recipe and hope my further creations are just as successful!

text:
Terrific is right! I make A LOT of chili once the weather starts cooling down, and frequently try new recipes, always searching for the perfect one.  This was definitely one of the best, if not the best, turkey chili I've made.  Not sure, but I'm guessing it had to do with the green chiles.  This recipe quick and easy, and unlike most chili/soups, it tasted excellent right away (versus tasting much better the 2nd day). I'll admit, I thought the method was a bit odd since most chili and soup recipes begin with sautÃ©ing the onions and peppers (and garlic, which this recipe doesn't use);  browning the meat, then combining the two  before you start adding everything else to the meat mix.  I stuck with the method in this recipe and it was fine. I did tweak this recipe to suit my own taste and am confident the changes didn't alter the original enough to affect, what I believe to be a 5 star recipe as written. Here are my tweaks: Added a can of red kidney and a can of black beans, both drained. Used 3 Tbsp of Bob Echol's taco seasoning mix (sans the red pepper flakes) instead of a box mix. Did not add additional oregano since my mix had it already, nor did I add red pepper flakes. No zucchini - can't imagine it in chili. Diced tomatoes instead of crushed. The finished product was delicious. It was a bit thick, but that's fixable. It was fine for eating right away, but will be super thick when re-heating. 3 people ate this and we only had 2 small servings left.

text:
I am not a chili fan, but was in charge of my team's submission for a Chili Cook off at work. Made this recipe for our practice run. Changed a few things, but it was a big hit for us. I eliminated the bell peppers, zucchini and green onions. (I don't do those). Used chicken broth vs. beef broth and added a drained can of black beans. I used 1/2 butter, 1/2 olive oil and sauteed the onions with a chopped garlic clove first, placed those aside, then browned the meat in the same skillet.  After the turkey was browned well with all spices, I added the prior onion/garlic, then added the rest of the ingredients. Put the mixture in the crock pot on high for 2.5-3 hrs. To add a little something after it cooked for an hour, I put about a teaspoon of soy sauce which seemed to blend all the flavors. Served with cheddar sprinkled on top, a spoon of sour cream and oyster crackers. It was the best and my family raved over it! Was a hit at the Chili Cook Off too.

text:
I'm not able to eat beans so this is the prefect recipe for me and also the first time I have cooked with ground turkey. In a slow cooker on auto shift I put the beef broth in and started to heat it up.  Cooked the ground turkey with the spices suggested in 1 TBSP of oil.  Set aside. With the other 1 TBSP oil sauteed the onions, 2 TBSP garlic, green bell pepper, and green chilies (med).  Added black bean and corn med salsa.  Heated a bit.  Added turkey mixture and salsa mixture to slow cooker.  Added 1-14 oz. can of whole kernel corn, drained and added diced chili tomatoes with 1/2 liquid.  Added 1 tsp chili powder and a dash of salt.  Cooked for 5 hours.  The family loved it and want me to serve it again.  Great way to use ground turkey. debmo

This was really good.  We don't care for zuchini, so we substituted a can of kidney and a can of pinto beans.  I used my own taco seasoning (from this website) and use anch chili powder (next time I will use regular chili powder).  We squeezed 1/4 of a juicy lime in each bowl and topped with fresh cilantro (we did not add the corriander), sour cream and shredded sharp cheddar cheese.  The lime and other toppings really made the dish.  It may have been a bit light on flavor otherwise.  Also it was good the first day; but, it was way better the second day.  If you are making this to take somewhere or for company make it the day before.  It is worth the wait.

We made this recipe to eat while we were watching the football playoffs. It's a nice meal for a chilly day. I didn't have chili pepper flakes, so I substitued chili powder in its place, about half a teaspoon. Also added a shake of cumin powder. The only other change I made was to add a can of black beans, and I would definitely do that again, added a lot in terms of flavor and thickening this up. The only other thing I would change is to cut back on the zucchini; for us this was way too much zucchini, and it seems a little out of place in a chili recipe. I would probably leave it out of the recipe entirely next time we make it. We topped ours with crushed tortilla chips, cheddar cheese and sour cream, and it was great.

Really Delicious. I had a packet of chilli seasoning mix on hand so I used that instead of taco mix. I also used 12 ounces of turkey and added a can of drained black beans. I browned the ground turkey on the stove top and then dumped that and everything else in the crock pot and cooked on high for about 4 1/2 hours. The chilli mix was just a tad too spicy so next time I'll use the taco mix as called for in the recipe

text:
Good!  I used the Taco Seasoning I recipe on this site instead of a package.  I didn't have all the ingredients for this on hand, so I used a fresh jalapeno instead of the canned chiles, I used some red and yellow bell pepper instead of green, and I left out the zucchini.  I used chunky chipotle salsa.  I added a little garlic, but other than that the amounts of spices were right on! (Usually I have to add more spices to make our household happy.)  Also, we like chili with beans, so I added one can of black beans and one can of kidney beans.  It probably doesn't compare to chili with beef and pork, but I'm giving it five stars because we ate all the leftovers, and that seldom happens.
